It is expected that the troops sent by this army to eastern Sichuan, such as Tian Songyao, Yang Sen, and Liu Cunhou, will be the general reserve force for bandit suppression. Yang Sen came to Chongqing a few days ago and has consulted in person on joint suppression. Everything is not a problem. (Special Dispatch, 8th)

Nanjing: Liu Xiang's representative, Fan Chongshi, said that the rumor that the two Lius have conflicts is inaccurate. Liu Xiang is now ordered to serve as the Commander-in-Chief of Bandit Suppression. From now on, he will concentrate his military strength, and the bandit forces will not be difficult to wipe out. However, the most worrying thing is the anti-tax army in Liu Wenhui's defense zone, because although its name is anti-tax, it is actually led by the Communist Party. The county magistrates in its defense zone who have been killed or expelled are countless. Huang Musong's Return to Nanjing Uncertain 69

Liu Shengzhen's Removal Still Pending

Beiping: Huang Musong is being monitored by Liu Wenlong and Sheng Shicai. Two of Huang's entourage have been killed. Huang's return to Nanjing is uncertain. (Special Dispatch, 7th)

Beiping: A telegram from Dihua states that Huang Musong's handling of new matters was improper, and all parties do not understand. Huang's attitude is negative. He will fly to Beijing as soon as the Eurasia aircraft arrives. The provincial capital is peaceful. (Special Dispatch, 7th)

Nanjing: The news that Huang Musong has temporarily lost his freedom seems to have been confirmed. Huang's return to Nanjing depends on Gong Bicheng and Peng Zhaoxian arriving in Xinjiang and reporting back before he can be sure. The mission of Gong and Peng is, on the one hand, to report the truth of the incident to the Central Government, and on the other hand, to explain the Central Government's trust to Liu Sheng. The Central Government will issue an order for Liu Shengzhen's removal as soon as it receives Gong and Peng's report and believes that Liu Sheng is sincere and that Huang's return to Nanjing is certain. (Special Dispatch, 8th)

Nanjing: The General Staff Department has held several emergency meetings to discuss response measures regarding the second Xinjiang incident. The department believes that

the situation in Xinjiang is extremely complicated recently. Analyzing its contents, the Hui rebellion that trapped the southern route of the Tianshan Mountains is one thing. Sheng and Liu's organization of a temporary government to replace the Jin family is another. Ma Zhongying's attempt to occupy territory and take the opportunity to advance westward is another. Ma Zhongying's troops were defeated by Sheng, but his remnants fled westward to Turpan, and the future troubles may not have ended. Moreover, the disorder in the southern route of the Tianshan Mountains remains the same. Therefore, it is believed that at this time of serious situation, it is difficult to achieve results without seeking fundamental solutions. Therefore, a decision has been made on a method, roughly to divide the north and south routes of the Tianshan Mountains and govern them separately, because the geology and customs of the two routes are different. Now that the situation in the northern Xinjiang has been roughly settled, the Central Government should immediately appoint Liu Sheng to manage military and civilian affairs. The provincial government should select local ethnic groups who have a reputation to participate in provincial affairs and establish a corresponding organization. (Special Dispatch, 8th)

Sino-Austrian Relations 86

Havas dispatch from Budapest, 7th. It is rumored that Hungary and Austria are in negotiations to restore close relations. These negotiations are being conducted by the delegations of the two countries attending the London Economic Conference. The Austrian delegation has submitted a formal proposal stating that Austria supports the Hungarian-Austrian customs union plan, advocating for the expansion of the existing commercial agreement between the two countries. Negotiations between the two sides are based on this proposal. This news has now been officially confirmed by Budapest. The Austrian proposal has been submitted to the Hungarian-Austrian Mixed Committee for review. This mixed committee is responsible for observing the development of commerce between the two countries. The Austrian proposal is largely favored by Hungary. The dispatch also stated, "The signing of the 'Eastern Locarno Treaty' is of no concern to those responsible in Hungary. This treaty only concerns Soviet Russia, as Soviet Russia wants to maintain its freedom of action in the Far East." (Note: The Eastern Locarno Treaty refers to a pact stipulating aggressor nations.)

Germany, Japan, and Persia Submit Amendments to British Disarmament Plan 87

National News Agency dispatch from Geneva, 7th. Germany, Japan, and Persia have submitted amendments to the League of Nations Secretariat regarding the British draft of the Disarmament Convention. Most of the amendments proposed by Germany concern troops stationed in distant colonies. According to the amendment, after the conclusion of this disarmament treaty, the troops stationed in colonies by various countries may only be used within the regions of those colonies and only for maintaining public order. Germany believes that within their own territories, countries should maintain reserves specifically for assisting colonial defense forces, and these reserves should also be regarded as colonial troops. The purpose of Germany's proposed amendment regarding colonial troops is aimed at France, fearing that France might mobilize millions of black troops from its colonies in wartime. Japan's proposal does not actually reduce armaments but increases them. Japan is demanding that the maximum caliber of land artillery be increased from 115 millimeters to 155 millimeters. Japan also opposes the provision in the British proposal that countries whose existing armaments exceed the specified maximum levels may temporarily retain them but may not increase them further. Japan is now demanding the abolition of this clause. In addition, Japan is also requesting that the maximum weight of tanks be increased from 16 tons to 20 tons. As for Persia's proposal, it calls for effective management of all arms manufacturing plants and arms trade in various countries.

Germany's Female Education Emphasizes Home Economics 88

(National News Agency dispatch from Berlin, 7th) The Prussian Ministry of Culture announced to the newspapers today that in the future, female education should focus on home economics, with science secondary. More schools will be established to train German girls to become virtuous housewives. Specialized schools will also be established to train talent for social work.

New Approach to Resolving Chahar Affairs 89

Urging Sun Dianying's Troops to Enter Qingdao

Pang and Feng's Troops Ordered to Enter Chahar

Special dispatch from Beiping. Regarding the Chahar affair, the central government repeatedly sent representatives to Zhangjiakou to meet with Feng Qinzhai to discuss a peaceful resolution. The point of contention between the two sides was whether or not Feng would abolish the name of the Anti-Japanese Allied Army. After Feng expressed that it would be difficult to abolish the name in the short term, adhering to the policy of preserving Chahar and resisting Japan, the Beiping authorities felt that the resolution was difficult. They then telegraphed the central government and Chairman Chiang Kai-shek for instructions. The reply telegram arrived in Beiping yesterday, advancing the third item in the previous three-item telegram (i.e., making necessary preparations to dispatch Pang Bingxun and Feng Qinzhai's troops to Chahar) to consolidate the Chahar region and prevent communization. After receiving the telegram, the Beiping authorities convened a meeting of generals such as Song Zheyuan, Pang Bingxun, and Feng Qinzhai at Jurentang yesterday afternoon (the 5th). It was decided to continue seeking a solution based on the principle of peace while making necessary preparations according to Chiang's instructions, urging Sun Dianying to leave Chahar from Suileng and enter Qingdao, and ordering Pang Bingxun and Feng Qinzhai to prepare to lead their troops into Chahar for defense. After the meeting, Pang Bingxun invited Hu Jiesan, the representative of Sun Dianying, to his private residence to discuss the matter that evening. Today (the 6th), Mr. Hu returned to Jurentang to meet with He, where discussions were held. The order for the entry of Pang and Feng's troops into Chahar was issued today (the 6th), preparing to concentrate their troops before the 8th. Once Sun's troops have departed, they will enter Chahar to take over the defense and advance forward. It is planned that Feng Qinzhai's troops will first open up Huailai, and Pang's troops will be stationed in the Chicheng Xuanhua area, advancing according to the situation. Since Sun Dianying was appointed as the Qinghai Western District Reclamation Commissioner, he has been preparing everything. However, due to issues such as military pay and departure routes, there have been slight delays. The current authorities have issued the fifth installment of military pay and two months' worth of provisions to the troops as needed for departure. Sun's troops have already decided to assemble the majority of their forces immediately, starting around the 10th to leave Chahar for Qinghai. It is expected that after Sun's troops have left, the defense areas of Sun's troops in the southern part of Chahar Province will be filled by the troops of Pang and Feng, as well as a portion of the central army. At that time, there will be new developments in the Chahar affair. The central government recently felt that the internal situation in Chahar Province was extremely complex, coupled with serious diplomatic issues. If further delays were to occur, they feared that there would be further complications in the future and felt increasingly棘手 (棘手 means thorny or troublesome). Therefore, they plan to resolve the matter as soon as possible. All parties, recognizing the seriousness of the situation in Chahar, are extremely anxious and are also working hard to make a final effort. Although Song Zheyuan feels that the situation is difficult, he still plans to send representatives to Chahar to meet with Feng. He has already telegraphed Deng Zhexi and Li Xin, who had gone to Tianjin, to return to Beiping to discuss everything and prepare to ask Deng and Li to go to Zhangjiakou again. At the same time, Zhao Pilian has arrived at Hebian Village to meet with Yan Xishan to discuss mediation methods. Recently, Yan Xishan will make a considerable statement to make a forceful effort. What the trend will be, in the near future, it might be revealed. (July 6)

The Case of the Theft of Hidden Gold from Kong Geng's Residence 91

The Hidden Gold in Kong's Residence Was Secretly Buried by the Former Owner

Recently Stolen by Neighbors, Kong Files a Protest

Hankou correspondence. A large-scale theft of hidden gold from the residence of former Provincial Committee Member Kong Geng recently occurred in Wuchang, creating a tense situation. For a time, it became the talk of the town. Since resigning from the Provincial Committee, Kong Geng has been living in Liangdao Street. His residence has another eastern courtyard inside the compound at No. 16 Xiaolou Lane, Liangdao Street. The west side door and the kitchen are between the original foundation of a temple room, with a brick wall built against the wall of the Peng family's residence. The two houses are connected. During the late Qing Dynasty, during the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom Rebellion, a man named Liu Changmao also joined the uprising. Later, he was recruited by the Qing court and surrendered to the Qing Dynasty. He acquired a large amount of gold, silver, and treasures during the chaos. After the rebellion was suppressed, he built houses on a large scale, extensively. At that time, the Qing court, in order to appease the rebels, was very lenient towards Liu and did not investigate deeply. To this day, many mansions and large houses in Wuchang are mostly Liu's legacy, sold by his descendants. The houses inhabited by Kong and Peng were also sold by Liu's family. When Liu was alive, he had a rich store of hidden gold, buried in various places. Because the matter was secret, he lost track of the locations. When he was on his deathbed, he revealed it to his family and instructed them to be careful to find it and not let it fall into the hands of outsiders.

The Peng brothers, the elder being Shisun and the younger being Younan, had heard this story. Recently, it is not known for what reason, they learned that there was a large amount of hidden treasure inside Kong's eastern courtyard. Therefore, using the name of repairing the wall, they secretly dug through Kong's courtyard wall, including the kitchen foundation, at night and discovered the hidden gold, taking it all away. The next morning, Kong learned of this and was very angry and protested. Peng initially denied it, but after repeated questioning, he finally admitted the truth. Peng, realizing that he was in the wrong, asked someone to apologize to Kong and admitted that he had dug up eight hundred ingots of silver, totaling more than four thousand taels, and was willing to return them to Kong for his disposal, to be used for educational and charitable purposes. However, Kong Geng, after surveying the excavated base, saw that the excavation was about seven feet wide, more than four zhang deep, and about one zhang deep. Based on the volume of the pit, he concluded that what they had obtained must be more than one hundred thousand taels of silver, definitely not just this amount. Therefore, he refused to accept Peng's terms. After repeated requests from the mediator, both parties agreed on two methods: (1) Temporarily use eight hundred ingots for educational and charitable purposes; (2) For those that have not been verified to be more than this number, they will be dealt with separately after verification. Later, the Peng brothers suddenly regretted their previous agreement and only offered seven hundred and sixty ingots to Kong Geng to donate to the Sanchu Middle School and other places, and widely published advertisements in various newspapers about the allocation of this money. As for the so-called second step, they were even less willing to give up what had come so easily and did not fulfill it. Kong Geng became even more angry and notified the mediator again, asking Peng to maintain his credibility, otherwise he would have to resort to the courts. The Peng brothers then gathered to discuss how to deal with the situation. According to the mediator, if they did not hand over the silver obtained in this case, they would have no peace. He advised them to offer some more to Kong for handling, but the Peng brothers insisted on refusing and published a notice denying the so-called second step, saying that all the silver dug up had been donated and that Kong Geng should not suddenly fabricate something out of nothing after a long time in an attempt to frame them. Kong Geng responded with a severe rebuttal and prepared everything to go to court.

As for how much silver Peng obtained, some say fifty thousand ingots, some say one hundred thousand, some say three hundred thousand, and some say that there were also gold bars, gold objects, gold leaves, and pearls. Opinions vary. Some say that the house is Liu's legacy, so the hidden treasure should belong to Liu. Liu's family, although they have no definite records due to the long time, are also collecting evidence and say that they already have some clues and will announce the truth soon. At the same time, citizens Sun and Tang of Wuchang, because the Peng brothers' actions were inappropriate, also held meetings to collectively request the authorities to order the Peng brothers to hand over all the hidden gold and use it for local charitable and public welfare purposes. It is rumored that Peng Younan has taken the money to Shanghai (some say to Hunan). Currently, Peng Shisun is facing Kong Geng with false pretenses. In addition to resorting to the courts, Kong has also requested the arrest of Peng, so this case has gradually expanded.

Page 12

Guangdong Province Continues to Purchase Aircraft 92

Ten Aircraft Recently Purchased from the United States

American Instructor Killed in Tragic Crash During Test Flight

Guangzhou correspondence. The Guangdong Provincial Air Force Headquarters, in order to implement its plan to expand the air force, plans to order more than a hundred aircraft in stages to equip the air force squadrons and strengthen its air power. Recently, it has purchased several batches of aircraft from foreign countries, each batch consisting of seven or eight or more than ten aircraft. The first phase of the aircraft purchase lottery issued by the Air Force Headquarters raised more than 400,000 yuan and was used to purchase three fighter planes, which arrived in the provincial capital on the 27th of the previous month. After assembly, they were test flown on the 1st of this month and were named the First, Second, and Third Aircraft Purchased with the First Phase of Lottery Funds. They were assigned to the Second Squadron for use as national defense fighter aircraft. In addition, the Municipal School Air Defense Association recently issued aircraft purchase lottery tickets to students throughout the city. After the conclusion, it raised more than 100,000 yuan. 100,000 yuan was first handed over to the First Army Group Headquarters to purchase an aircraft, which has also been delivered. It is named "Municipal School" and was test flown today. It was also learned that a total of ten aircraft arrived from Hong Kong on the 27th, excluding three lottery aircraft and one Municipal School aircraft, there were also six fighter planes purchased by the government for national defense. After this batch of new aircraft was assembled, the Air Force sent personnel to test the speed and components. At 10:20 AM on the 1st of this month, an American instructor, 士, a senior advisor and flying instructor of the Air Force Headquarters, was piloting a newly arrived fighter plane (biplane, painted silver-gray, valued at approximately HK$180,000) from the Shougouling airfield. Initially, it was intended to demonstrate flying skills during the test flight. Unexpectedly, less than forty minutes after takeoff, after rising to approximately 1,400 feet, just as it was circling the airfield, the aircraft suddenly descended rapidly from the sky as if it had completely lost its ability to maneuver. In an instant, the aircraft crashed next to the aircraft hangar. The entire aircraft was destroyed into pieces. The American instructor's legs were broken, and he suffered severe injuries to the lower body. He died on the spot. Upon hearing this alarming news, the Air Force Headquarters sent personnel to rescue, but it was too late. The Yueguang Funeral Company was hired to inspect and enshroud the body of the American instructor. It was learned that the American instructor, 士, had extensive experience in flying. He had served as a flying squadron leader in the United States. He came to Guangdong to serve under the invitation of the Air Force Headquarters for only three months. Three other Americans came with 士, one teaching aerial bombing, one teaching aerial machine gunning, and 士 teaching aerial reconnaissance. 士's wife is an American movie star. The couple were very affectionate. She only came to China last month and lost her husband in less than a month. She mourned over the body yesterday and fainted repeatedly. It is said that 士's wife has decided to transport her husband's remains back to the United States. The Air Force Department is purchasing a coffin worth 900 yuan for a dignified burial. (4th)

This treasury bond has a face value of one national currency yuan per bill, with cash as a reserve fund, and can be cashed at any time. To facilitate the uniformity of revenue and expenditure, all payment of taxes, salaries, military pay, and all public funds can be used. This treasury bond is not registered. If lost or damaged, it will not be replaced. The government may fully recover all of them if necessary. It is said that the regulations for issuing treasury bonds have been approved at the provincial affairs meeting. (June 29)

Hunan Provincial Government Reports on the Severity of the Flood Disaster 94

Disaster Area Spreads to More Than Thirty Counties

More Than Two Hundred Villages Submerged in Lake Areas

Changsha correspondence. Since the beginning of summer this year, Hunan Province has experienced continuous rain and mountain floods. In addition, the huge flood of the Yangtze River flowed back into Dongting Lake, and many embankments in the lake areas were submerged and breached. The severity of the disaster is the same as in 1931. In total, the disaster area reaches more than thirty counties, and more than two hundred villages have been submerged. Hunan Provincial Governor He Jian, in addition to instructing the Department of Civil Affairs and the Provincial Relief Association to send personnel to the counties to investigate and expedite emergency relief with local officials and gentry, believes that the province has suffered repeated disasters, the people's strength has been depleted for a long time, and the bandit suppression is underway, and the treasury is extremely exhausted. Yesterday, he specially compiled the actual situation of the Hunan disaster and submitted it to the central government, requesting relief to alleviate the suffering. The original telegram read, "Chairman Lin of the National Government, Premier Wang of the Executive Yuan, Chairman Xu of the Relief Committee, may you be blessed, your benevolent words are beneficial and widespread, I dare not delay. Hunan Province has complex rivers and crisscrossing lakes. Whenever the rivers and lakes rise, there is a risk of embankment breaches. This government, in order to prevent problems before they occur, has already instructed the Department of Civil Affairs to strictly order the counties to strengthen protection and sent personnel to inspect separately. However, since the beginning of summer, there has been continuous rain for more than a month, and mountain floods have occurred. The Xiang, Zi, Yuan, and Li rivers have all risen at the same time. In addition, the huge flood of the Yangtze River flowed back into Dongting Lake. Since May 19, according to the Changsha Customs water level marker, the water level has reached more than three zhang, which is almost the same as the water level in 1931. The counties reporting the disaster situation are sending documents in succession, and we are overwhelmed. Now, in summary, the counties with severe damage to houses and loss of life of humans and animals include Hengyang, Chen County, Xiangtan, Xiangxiang, Hengshan, Taiyang, Changsha, Xinhua, Liuyang, Anhua, Taoyuan, Sangzhi, Mayang, Baojing, Xupu, Guzhang, Yuanling, Fenghuang, and Tongdao, a total of 19 counties. The embankments that have been breached are in 11 counties, including 88 villages breached in Changde, 51 villages breached and 2 villages submerged in Yuanjiang, 7 villages breached in Hanshou, 8 villages breached and 19 villages submerged in Lai County, 9 villages breached and 3 villages submerged in Nan County, 9 villages breached in Xiangyin, 6 villages breached and 5 villages submerged in Huarong, 10 villages breached in Yueyang, 2 villages breached and 6 villages submerged in Yiyang, 70% of the villages in Anxiang submerged, and 12 embankment breaches in Linxiang. The extent of the disaster and the magnitude of the losses are the same as in 1931. In addition to instructing the Department of Civil Affairs to work with the members of the Provincial Relief Association to rush to the affected counties to conduct a thorough investigation and consult with local officials and gentry to jointly plan emergency relief, and ordering the county magistrates to supervise their subordinates day and night to rescue, this province has been suffering from repeated disasters, and is also in the midst of bandit suppression. The treasury is exhausted, the officials are hungry, the people have been exhausted for a long time, and there are starving people everywhere. Now that this great disaster has come, we can only sigh with regret. I, Jian, am serving as the governor and have encountered a year of misfortune. I am heartbroken and exhausted. I can only present my insignificant words, hoping for the grace of saving lives. I am moved to tears, and I pay my respects to your benevolence. He Jian, Governor of Hunan Province, bows and seals," (July 4)

Academia Sinica to Excavate Ancient Relics in Linzi 95

Searching for Items from Before the Zhou Dynasty

Planning to Start Work After the Autumn Cooling

Jinan correspondence. Linzi County in Qingzhou Province is the ancient capital of the State of Qi during the Spring and Autumn period. Duke Tai was enfeoffed in Yingqiu, which is located here. Although the era is far away this year, the remains can still be faintly seen. Shang tripods, Zhou pans, Han tiles, and Qin bricks are often discovered by woodcutters and shepherds. After excavating the Yin Ruins the year before last, Academia Sinica decided to continue excavating in Shandong because the Qi capital of Linzi is of great importance to Chinese culture. Fearing that they would not have a clear idea of where to begin, they first excavated the ancient capital of the State of Tan in the Spring and Autumn period near Longshan Town in the east of Jinan as a trial.

The results were good. Academia Sinica then decided to realize its Linzi excavation plan this year. Recently, Dong Zuobin was first sent to Linzi to conduct a field investigation. Dong returned to Jinan yesterday. According to his talk, the most famous ancient site in Linzi is the ancient city of Qi. There are two ancient cities. The outer city is forty li in circumference and was built later by the State of Qi. The inner city is the old site of Yingqiu, and the remains of the city walls still exist. In addition, there are ancient tombs such as those of Tian Dan and Yan Ying, which are related to ancient culture. Academia Sinica has decided to go to Linzi this autumn to excavate the ancient city of Yingqiu first, with the greatest purpose of searching for items from the Stone Age before the Zhou Dynasty. Because the items discovered in Linzi after the Zhou Dynasty are not unique, the pottery shards and mud seals discovered on the ground are all from later periods. However, no Stone Age items have been discovered so far. If nothing is found in Yingqiu City, they will excavate the outer city. If nothing is found in the outer city, they will have to excavate elsewhere, because the locals say that there is another Yingqiu City elsewhere. It is difficult to judge where the real Yingqiu is. As for other ancient tombs, they plan not to excavate them for the time being. The reason is that the tombs of Tian Dan and others are said to have been robbed long ago, and the academy has adopted the principle of "work if possible, preserve if not." They are especially unwilling to hastily excavate tombs. (6th)

Shen Honglie's Political Achievements 96

Overview of Qingdao City in the Past Year

People from All Walks of Life Actively Urge Him to Stay

Qingdao correspondence. Since the news of Shen Honglie's resignation came out, people from all walks of life have been urging him to stay, because Shen's political achievements in Qingdao are quite remarkable. Looking back on the year and a half that Shen has been in charge of Qingdao, the city's construction projects include the construction of Pier No. 5, which cost 4 million yuan, the construction of the Xiaogang Shipyard, which cost nearly 300,000 yuan, and the completion of the Qianhai Pier and the Huiquan Sports Field, which cost more than 200,000 yuan each. The expansion of roads has made it possible for cars to reach dozens of miles outside the city. In addition, Qingdao City is often plagued by the influx of Changshan water in the summer. Shen ordered the Public Works Bureau to actively cover the sewer pipes to prevent flooding from now on. With regard to fire prevention, in view of the fact that someone was careless last year, resulting in the burning and death of seven people due to the burning of the staircase, Shen ordered all wooden stairs in the city to be rebuilt as cement stairs, to be completed within one year, and the reconstruction is underway. As for public security, robbery has not been seen for several months, and the police have been able to be honest and diligent. Other achievements include increasing the number of schools to prevent children from dropping out of school and building hundreds of houses for civilians in the east and west ridges, benefiting the poor. Recently, he has also been planning to establish an agricultural and industrial bank to relieve the difficulties of the common people. These are all his achievements. Shen usually treats naval soldiers very well, but is very strict with officers. The recent assassination attempt on Shen by Feng Zhichong was caused by the seduction of two or three unscrupulous officers. The rumor that Shen intercepted military pay is completely false. The people have telegraphed the central government and the Beiping branch to urge him to stay. The elders and representatives of the people went to the city government the day before yesterday to earnestly ask Shen to dismiss his intention to resign. However, Shen's intention to resign has not been dismissed. Therefore, the people of the city will hold a city residents' conference on the 8th to make a large-scale effort to urge him to stay.

The Sichuan Army's Chaotic War Begins 97

Liu and Deng's joint attack on the north of Chengdu intensifies; many 24th Army generals advocate for Liu Wenhui's resignation.

Xu's bandits and Tian's army are locked in a stalemate; anti-tax forces rise up like swarms of bees.

Representatives of Sichuan's various institutions and legal groups appeal for peace.

Hankou Correspondence: After Liu Xiang issued a telegram proclaiming his aim to unify Sichuan and eliminate the Red bandits, he advanced to Longchang and deployed military forces. The situation between Qianwei, Jiajiang, Renshou, and Jingyan suddenly deteriorated. Liu Wenhui was particularly determined to seek revenge and personally went to Jiading to command. He specially appointed Xiang Yuren as the rear guard commander, stationed in Chengdu. He then dedicated his main force to the southern front. The second major conflict between the two Lius is about to begin. When Liu Xiang departed for Longchang, Deng Xihou, Tian Songyao, Liu Cunhou, and Yang Sen all sent liaison officers to accompany him. All armies would obey his orders. Liu Xiang, now the leader of the alliance, was full of confidence. He ordered his troops to concentrate at designated locations, awaiting the order to launch a general offensive. He also telegraphed Deng Xihou to attack from Pihe and requested Tian Songyao, Liu Cunhou, and Yang Sen to focus on defending key fortresses to prevent bandits from advancing south. Upon receiving Liu's telegram, Deng was greatly encouraged. On the 2nd, he advanced to Jintang and launched a major counter-offensive against the 24th Army. Fierce battles have been raging in the Ban Zhuyuan and Zhaojiadu areas for days. The 24th Army, as an isolated force, struggling to support both north and south, felt overwhelmed. Except for the army commander Liu Wenhui, who remained stubbornly resistant, determined to make a desperate stand, many of his generals wanted to preserve their strength and were unwilling to sacrifice. A few days ago, Liu convened a military meeting in Chengdu, where Chen Hongwen, Wang Yuanhu, and Peng Fu all suggested that Liu temporarily step down to ease tensions from all sides, indicating the perilousness of their situation. Amidst this chaotic war between the armies, anti-tax forces rose up like swarms of bees in various counties. The magistrate of Qionglai County has already been arrested and killed. Xu Xiangqian's bandit forces are particularly rampant. According to various reports, they have already occupied seven counties and are continuing to advance south. They have also ordered He's bandits in western Hubei to quickly infiltrate southern Sichuan and establish contact. The official sources only acknowledge the loss of Tongjiang, Nanjiang, Bazhong, and Guangyuan counties and claim that Tian's army has recovered Guangyuan. Attempting to defeat a formidable enemy with exhausted troops and hastily claiming to have recovered lost territory will not be so easy. On the 5th, a gentleman traveled from Chengdu via Chongqing to Hankou. According to him, the Red bandit forces are expanding daily. Tian's army is currently holding the line along the Cangxi, Yilong, and Guangyuan rivers, confronting the bandits but have not yet launched a counter-offensive.

Representatives from various Sichuan provincial institutions and legal groups, including Zeng Jian and 1,900 others, issued a joint telegram appealing for peace, deeply saddened by the resurgence of Red bandits and the outbreak of internal war. The original text is recorded below: "Since the great war last year in Sichuan, the people have suffered terribly and been displaced, beyond description. Unexpectedly, before their shock has subsided, war has broken out again. If circumstances permitted and the war was justified, the people could temporarily endure it. But now, the Red bandits are rampant, like a raging tide. Tongjiang, Nanjiang, Bazhong, and other counties have been lost and then regained. Guangyuan, Cangxi, Yilong, Langzhong, and other counties have successively fallen. Bandit gangs everywhere are again raising red flags, engaging in arson and looting. Danger lurks on all sides, and perilous situations abound. Last year, the military leaders put forward a plan for governing Sichuan. The people hoped that the end of the internal war would allow its implementation. But the armies' words and actions contradict each other, becoming even more extreme, levying exorbitant taxes and focusing their attacks on the people, thus creating opportunities for the Red bandits. If they urgently change course and work together to suppress the bandits, it might not spread beyond control. But instead, they turn their weapons against each other, as if bearing deep hatred, focusing on internal strife and abandoning the responsibility of suppressing bandits. They call it 'unifying first and then suppressing the Reds,' but in reality, unification may not be achieved, and the Red scourge is spreading like wildfire. The 70 million people of Sichuan are trapped in an irrecoverable situation. Moreover, if the armies were to unanimously suppress the Reds, supporting each other and moving from disunity to unity, it would be an excellent opportunity for the unification of Sichuan. Ignoring this and engaging in internal strife, how can they excuse themselves from the condemnation of their conscience? Jian and others, with their remaining years, are alarmed by the impending disaster. Therefore, we tearfully implore fellow countrymen across the nation to provide assistance and rescue, and earnestly request the Central Government to send special commissioners to Sichuan immediately to effectively stop the Sichuan war, strictly order all troops to focus on suppressing the Reds, and cooperate fully to achieve complete success. Perhaps the dying people of Sichuan will have a chance to survive. Otherwise, the entire province will fall to Red control, causing even more harm than in Jiangxi. If the Red bandits gain this strategic region, the disaster will spread to the entire nation. If attempts to recover are made only then, it will be too late. The situation is urgent, and we hereby express our lament. We hope you will consider it. Respectfully, Zeng Jian, Xu Jiong, Pei Gang, Xu Xiaogang, Yin Changheng, Chen Guodong, Peng Guanglie, Du Wenyuan, and 1,900 other representatives from various institutions and legal groups in Sichuan." (5th)

(Songjiang)

Establishing a Time Epidemic Hospital 98

Zhang Shaoxiu, director of the Songjiang County Hospital, believing that the summer season has arrived, in order to prevent epidemic diseases, convened representatives of various institutions for a preparatory meeting. More than 20 people attended, including district chief Zhong Taishi. Zhang Shaoxiu, as chairman, reported on the process of convening the meeting. After discussion, all agreed that this year, instead of establishing a separate epidemic hospital, a new ward of the hospital should be designated as an epidemic department, with a branch outside the West Gate, to provide swift medical care. The expenses are temporarily set at 1,000 yuan. The hospital will prepare a donation registry and submit it to the county government for sealing and distribution for fundraising. It was unanimously approved to officially open on the 20th of this month. The hospital will immediately begin preparations.

Change of leadership at the People's Education Center 99

Shen Benqian, director of the People's Education Center of the County Education Bureau, has served for several years and has carefully planned, making many contributions to people's education. He has now resigned to take up an editorial position at a publishing house in Shanghai. Unable to retain him, Director Zhu selected and recommended Lu Dingrong to fill the vacancy. He took over the position at the center yesterday.

(Taicang) Tiger Plague Discovered in Shaxi Town 100

The summer season has arrived, and the tiger plague has returned, with a fierce and untreatable outbreak. Mr. Zhu Jingzhi, the current head of the Shaxi Town Defense Corps, suddenly suffered from severe vomiting and diarrhea around 10 AM the day before. Due to the severity of the onset, despite various diagnoses and treatments by famous Chinese and Western doctors, nothing worked. He passed away around 5 PM that afternoon. Another prominent figure in Shaxi has passed away.

(Suzhou) Large-scale reassignment of trial judges at the High Court 101

The High Court announced on the 8th that Jiang Youhua, a trial judge from Lianshui County, has been transferred to the province to await new assignment. Liu Kanyong has been appointed to act as his replacement. Shi Wending, a trial judge from Jinshan County, and Wang Enpei, a trial judge from Jiangyin County, have been reassigned to each other's positions. Lu Binglin, a trial judge from Tai County, has been transferred to the province, with Gao Weiju, a trial judge from Chuansha County, appointed to take over his position. Yuan Wencheng has been appointed to act as his replacement in Chuansha. Zheng Ligeng, a jailer from Nanhui, has been transferred to the province, with Ding Zhaowei, an officer from the High Court's detention center, appointed to replace him. The newly appointed warden of the Jiangning Court detention center, Cheng Zhenlin, visited President Lin at the High Court on the 8th and will soon depart for Nanjing to take up his new post.

(Wuxi) Summary of the Rice Industry Members' General Meeting 102

The Wuxi Rice and Bean Industry Association held a joint executive and supervisory committee meeting on the 20th of the previous month, resolving to change the existing 0.99 discount for agency sales of various businesses to 0.984 and setting July 1st as the implementation date. However, businesses in the Beitang and Huangniqiao sections strongly opposed this, while the Sanliqiao section absolutely supported it. Both sides went to extremes, and no agreement could be reached. Therefore, yesterday afternoon at 3 PM, the association convened a general meeting of members of the eight sections. Chairman Zhao Zixin presided over the meeting, resolving the following: 1) The case of the dispute over changing to a 0.984 discount was reviewed and passed as originally planned. 2) There are many obstacles to using the new system of weights and measures, and a postponement is requested. 3) Regarding the provincial order to ban brokers to eliminate harm to farmers, each section should submit a written opinion to the meeting for review and transfer. 4) Nineteen preparatory committee members were appointed to prepare for the re-election of executive and supervisory committee members. 5) The case of levying customs duties on imported food from abroad to prevent dumping should be submitted to the Jiangsu Ninghu Municipal and County Rice Industry Association for forwarding to the central authorities for approval.

(Nantong) Suspension of marine product education tax 103

The Nantong County Education Bureau levies a marine product education tax in Lusi on the Yellow Sea coast. The Ministry of Industry and Commerce has consulted the Jiangsu Provincial Government, stating that although the collection of the marine product education tax in Nantong is necessary to revitalize fishermen's education, it is inconsistent with the central government's clear order to exempt fishery taxes and is difficult to approve. The Provincial Government has ordered the County Government to immediately suspend the tax.

Lüsi Hurricane Disaster 104

In Lüsi on the Yellow Sea coast, a hurricane passed through the area at 9 a.m. on the 6th, collapsing houses and injuring people, causing a major disaster.

(Jiangyin) Verdict in the private production of counterfeit pills case 105

Lu Hualin, a bailiff of the county government, and Xuan Xingbao, a member of the detective team, discovered Xiong Kaiyuan, Jin Kunpei, and others on the 6th on the Hongqiao Riverbank, privately producing Hangzhou Hu Qing Yu Tang Ginseng Rejuvenation Pills. They also found counterfeit pill pamphlets and woodcut blocks. On the 7th, the Public Security Bureau transferred the case to the county. After questioning by trial judge Wang, the evidence was found to be conclusive. Xiong Kaiyuan was sentenced to two months in prison, and Jin Kunpei was fined 40 yuan. The counterfeit pills were handed over to the Physicians' Association for testing.

(Yangzhou)

Danger to the embankments in the Third District, an order to stop ferry service 106

The third district of this county is located on the Jiangbian River, in the lower reaches, and its embankments along the river have recently been threatened by the flooding of the Yangtze River from the upper reaches. The district chief of the district, Tao Hongru, has specially requested Magistrate Ma to order all ferries in the Jiajiang River to stop operating to protect the embankments. Yesterday, the county sent a telegram to the Zhenjiang Customs Superintendent, approving that the Ningkou and Zhenmiao ferries should be ordered to temporarily suspend operations during periods of dangerous water levels.

(Xiaoshan)

Robbery and Injury on the West Xiaojiang Bank 107

In Luoshan Township on the West Xiaojiang Bank in Xiaoshan, a family surnamed Shen was robbed by more than a dozen bandits who broke into their house on the evening of the 6th of this month. All their belongings, including a string of pearls, four gold rings, and two boxes of clothing, were stolen. At the time, a neighbor, Wu Xiaocai, sounded the alarm, but was shot in the chest by a bandit, hitting a vital spot and killing him instantly. Subsequently, a nearby water police patrol boat arrived after hearing the alarm, but the bandits had already fled.

(Hangzhou) Fire at Bingxiang Lane, Hushu 108

A fire broke out at the home of Chen Shen at No. 5 Bingxiang Lane, Hushu, Hangzhou, at 1:40 p.m. yesterday, due to unattended cooking. Smoke billowed in the sky, and the fire was intense. Fortunately, firefighters from the fire department arrived one after another and made every effort to put out the fire. It only lasted for 30 minutes. Three households were burned down: No. 4, Yin Chengfa; No. 5, Chen Shen; and No. 6, Zhang Shounong. Several houses in the affected fire lane were damaged, including No. 2, an empty house; No. 3, Ding Yuanxing, a funeral supply store; and No. 7, the Sanbao Township Office. The police brought the fire starter in for questioning. The loss is estimated at about 2,000 yuan.

Local News

General Li Du Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday 109

Will Rest Briefly in Shanghai Before Going to Beijing and Jiangxi to Report

Expresses a Thorough Determination to Resist Japan and Not Take Any Position, Details Retreat from Russia, Will Host Reporters Today

General Li Du, Commander-in-Chief of the Jilin Self-Defense Army and a stalwart fighter against Japan, accompanied by his secretary Liu Xubo and interpreter Liu Guanren, returned to the country aboard the Italian postal ship Conte Verde from Venice, Italy. The ship arrived at the port at 12:45 p.m. yesterday and docked at the Qichang Wharf in Pudong. Representatives from all sectors of the city went to welcome him. Mr. Li stated that he would rest briefly in Shanghai before going to Beijing to report to the Central Government on his anti-Japanese experiences and that he would host the press at 2 p.m. today. Details are as follows:

(Welcome from All Sectors)

Those who went to the port to welcome him yesterday included Li Dachao, Section Chief of the Municipal Government; Xie Chuanda, Director of General Affairs; Hu Haishan, Captain of the Water Patrol Team of the Public Security Bureau; Dong Pingyu, Deputy Inspector General; Wu Huanzhang, representative of Ma Zhanshan; Wang Erzhan, representative of Su Bingwen; Zhou Weitai, former Director of the Industry Bureau of Heilongjiang; Pu Bingshan, Xu Haiting, Lang Guanpu, and Jiang Songnian, officers from the Ma and Su units; Li Yulin, younger brother of General Li; Ye Jiaxing, of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce; Zhu Xuefan, of the General Labor Union; Chen Yafu and Chu Huiseng, of the Northeast Volunteer Army Support Association; Hu Fengxiang, Zhang Yichen, Chen Binghui, Wang Hesong, Liu Zhongying, and Zheng Dongshan of the First Special District Citizens' Association and various branch associations; and over a hundred newspaper reporters.

(Arrival Situation)

The Conte Verde entered the port at 11 a.m. yesterday and docked at the Qichang Wharf in Pudong at 12:45 p.m. The Municipal Government representative Li Dachao and the Public Security Bureau Deputy Inspector General Dong Pingyu and others took the Public Security Bureau ferry from Pier No. 10 in Nanshi at 12:00 noon to welcome them. The other welcoming representatives from various organizations took small passenger ferries from the Jianghai Customs Pier to Pudong. After General Li Du shook hands and exchanged greetings with the welcoming personnel and reporters on the ship, he and the Municipal Government representative Li Dachao took the Public Security Bureau ferry, disembarking at the Nanshi Guanqiao Pier at 2:05 p.m. and took a car to the China Hotel on Guizhou Road to rest. The Public Security Bureau sent a water patrol team to guard the Qichang Wharf in Pudong and a police brigade to guard the Nanshi Guanqiao Pier.

(Li's Demeanor)

General Li is 53 years old, wearing a light gray suit. He is burly, his hair is already gray, but his spirit is very strong. He is humble in attitude and expresses many emotions. Accompanying General Li this time are his secretary Liu Xubo and interpreter Liu Guanren, as well as Liu Piguang, Wang Ziyao, and Jiang Ying, his representatives stationed in Shanghai, who came from Shanghai to Hong Kong to welcome him. Wang Delin is still in Hong Kong and did not come with them.

(Anti-Japanese Experiences)

General Li met with reporters from various newspapers on the ship yesterday. According to him, he fought against Japan in the Northeast for thirteen months, from Harbin to Mishan. He experienced more than a hundred battles, large and small, and held eight counties for more than eight months. Currently, a part of his troops is still remaining in hiding in Jilin Province. Recently, they occupied four counties, including Mishan, Baoqing, Hulin, and Raohe. Dongning has also been occupied by Wang Delin's forces.

(Reasons for Retreating to Russia)

On January 6th of this year, I was stationed in Mishan City, commanding my troops. There was a fierce battle about 160 li near Mishan. On the 8th, the enemy troops used 117 armored vehicles to detour to the rear of our army, launching an attack, causing us to be cut off from both the front and the rear. I led a company of guards and broke through the encirclement. Seeing that the situation was dire and there was nothing I could do, I reluctantly retreated into Russian territory on the 9th.

(Six Months of Travel)

From the time I left the country to the time I returned, it took a total of six months. I stayed in the Soviet Union for three months. My nerves became abnormal due to stimulation, so I was accompanied by medicine every day. Then I went to Berlin for medical treatment, staying for half a month. Later, I went to Rome to recuperate for a month. The rest of the time was spent traveling. The troops who retreated into Russian territory with me have all returned to the country via Xinjiang, totaling about 7,000 people. They are currently stationed temporarily in Xinjiang Province, guarding the border.

(Impressions of European Travel)

The Soviet Union's first five-year plan has been successful, and the second five-year plan has already begun. The people's lives are quite difficult, but they are working extremely hard on construction, which is admirable. German Chancellor Hitler is highly trusted and respected by the people of the whole country. Members of the National Socialist Party are all over the country, and the swastika symbol is everywhere. Italian Prime Minister Mussolini is truly a patriot. I met with him in Italy. Italy's construction in the past ten years has progressed rapidly, thanks to Mussolini's efforts.

(Meeting with Zhang)

I met with Zhang Xueliang many times in Rome. Zhang has decided to stay in Rome for three months before going to other countries for inspection. Zhang's body has now recovered, returning to the state it was in before 1925.

(Ding Chao Captured)

General Ding Chao, with his indomitable spirit, fought to the death with Japanese and puppet troops. During the battle in Baoqing, because General Ding refused to retreat, he was eventually captured by the Japanese army. He was first sent to Harbin, and then to Changchun. When I arrived in Russia, I heard that the puppet organization had issued an amnesty order and intended to reuse General Ding. But General Ding ultimately refused to be lured by benefits and expressed his refusal. There was then talk of his being harmed. To this day, news is silent, but whether the rumors of Ding's death are true has not been confirmed.

(Future Actions)

Since the signing of the Tanggu Truce, the anti-Japanese military affairs have come to an end. My return to the country this time is to handle the aftermath. As for my anti-Japanese stance, it remains unchanged. I will rest briefly in Shanghai before going to Beijing to report to the Central Government on my anti-Japanese experiences. Then I will go to Jiangxi to pay respects to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek. In the future, I plan to come to Shanghai to recuperate and do not want to take any position. Most Chinese people value their personal lives and property more than the country and the nation. I deeply hope that the Chinese people will correct their mistakes in the future and always put the country and the nation first, and catch up quickly, it is not too late.

(Ma and Su Visit)

After Mr. Li arrived at the China Hotel at 2:40 p.m., Public Security Bureau Chief Wen Hongen visited him and left after talking for about ten minutes. At about 3 p.m., General Ma Zhanshan visited with Zhang Dianjiu, and General Su Bingwen also arrived soon after. They exchanged detailed opinions on the issue of post-war arrangements for their subordinates. Ma, Su, and others did not depart until after an hour.

(Banquet Last Night)

Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin, and others hosted a banquet for Mr. Li at their residence in Haig Road at 7 p.m., and invited Ma Zhanshan and Su Bingwen to accompany him. At that time, toasts were made and songs were sung until about 9 p.m., when the gathering dispersed in joy.

Mr. Li plans to stay in Shanghai for a week and then go to Beijing to report everything to the Central Government. He will then go to Jiangxi to pay respects to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek and report on his anti-Japanese experiences. Mr. Li has also scheduled a meeting with reporters from various newspapers at the Cangzhou Hotel on Jing'an Temple Road at 2 p.m. today to report on his detailed experiences in the war against Japan, it is said.

Newly Appointed Hubei Provincial Chairman Zhang Qun Reluctantly Accepts Position 110

Will Go to Take Office in Mid-Month

Will Go to Beijing in the Coming Days to Consult on Everything

The newly appointed Chairman of the Hubei Provincial Government, Zhang Qun, is currently staying in Shanghai and plans to go to Beijing in the coming days to consult with the Central Government on everything. He will be able to go to Hubei Province to take office in mid-month. According to Mr. Zhang, he told visiting reporters that the Central Government had firmly requested him to take the position of Chairman of Hubei Province,

Because Yu Cai was unable to overcome, he had to refuse to refuse. As for the candidates for the Provincial Committee and the heads of various departments, the Central Government should determine them. He will go to Beijing in the coming days to consult with the Central Government on everything, or may turn to Jiangxi to pay respects to Chiang Kai-shek, and will go to Hubei Province before the 20th of this month. The long-term impact of the Red bandits and floods in Hubei Province has made it difficult to carry out reforms in the provincial departments. The total tax revenue of the province is only about 400,000 yuan per month, or only five or six million yuan per year, which is not as much as the revenue of Shanghai City. The monthly expenditure is close to one million yuan, and the Central Government now provides a monthly subsidy of 600,000 yuan, which is enough to offset the revenue and expenditure.

After Inspecting Japanese Industry

Will Return to Java via the Philippines

Yesterday's Meeting of the City Chamber of Commerce Executive Committee 115

Discussed Cases Handed Down from the General Assembly

The Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce held its tenth Executive Committee meeting yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM. Attendees included Wang Xiaolai, Ma Jiliang, Ye Jiaxing, Zheng Zenan,

Pan Xusheng, Wang Yansong, Lu Wenshao, Luo Qinghua, Pei Yunqing, Fang Jiaobo, Chen Songyuan, Lao Jingxiu, and others. Wang Xiaolai chaired the meeting, with Yan Esheng as the recording secretary. The following cases were discussed: 1. Discussion of cases handed down from the fourth General Assembly: A. Implementing the resolution from the previous session to promote domestic goods, starting with an investigation and imposing appropriate sanctions on those who violate the resolution based on the severity of the circumstances (proposed by the Joint Supervisory Committee). B. Proposing that the City Chamber of Commerce lead various trade associations to quickly establish a general organization for resisting foreign goods and effectively protect the inspection teams of various industries (proposed by the Trade Association). C. Merchants and groups that promote the sales of Japanese goods should know to be ashamed and reflect on their actions; please discuss measures at the General Assembly and plan for future actions (proposed by the Copper, Iron, and Machinery Trade Association). It was resolved to hand this over to the Domestic Goods Promotion Committee to actively proceed according to the methods of Case A. D. Organizing committees for: 1. Commerce, 2. Seven Industries, 3. Financial Enterprises, 4. Research on Industrial and Commercial Laws and Regulations (proposed by Executive Committee member Wang Yansong). It was resolved to first submit the nominations to the Standing Committee and then submit them to the Executive Committee for approval. E. Proposing that the central government be requested to stop provinces and cities from setting up taxes similar to "lijin" after the abolition of "lijin," and proposing the establishment of a specialized committee on tax research by this Chamber of Commerce (proposed by the Standing Committee). F. Requesting the amendment of the import tariff regulations to include a clause allowing customs to inspect stores at any time (proposed by the Clock and Watch Trade Association). G. Requesting an increase in the import tax on sulfuric acid (proposed by Fang Yexie and Xiao Chu). H. Regarding the affixing of stamp taxes, the types of accounting books that must have stamps affixed should be determined, and searches must be conducted through legal procedures. It is proposed that a committee be organized by this Chamber of Commerce to handle this matter (proposed by the Standing Committee). The above four cases were discussed together, and it was resolved to petition the central government to order the prohibition of provinces and cities from establishing new taxes similar to "lijin." As for the candidates for the specialized committee, they will be determined by the Standing Committee and then submitted to the Executive Committee for approval. Cases F, G, and H will be handled after the establishment of the specialized committee. I. The Commerce Section should handle company and trademark registrations on behalf of merchants, as well as company and business registration of seals to facilitate merchants and also for review (proposed by Executive Committee member Wang Yansong). It was resolved to have the Commerce Section handle this and set the handling fees as follows: 1. Business registration: 20 yuan; 2. Trademark registration: 30 yuan per item; 3. Company registration: 50 yuan. Members of the Chamber of Commerce and members of affiliated trade associations will receive a 50% discount. J. The membership fees paid by trade associations to the Chamber of Commerce each session should be based on the actual amount of the member's capital in the most recent year as the standard for collecting membership fees (proposed by the Postal Industry Association). It was resolved to have the Commerce Section handle this. K. Establishing an Industry Regulations Enforcement Committee (proposed by Cheng Yujie). It was resolved to petition the Social Affairs Bureau to request that an Industry Regulations Enforcement Committee be jointly established by various institutions, following the model of the Labor-Management Arbitration Committee. L. Leading various trade associations to quickly organize a rayon manufacturing plant (proposed by Feng Shao, et al.). It was resolved to notify various trade associations that they should actively promote the organization of factories for raw materials, such as rayon yarn factories. (4) Discussed the request by Committee Member Zheng Zenan to exempt the sugar industry from wharfage fees and reduce dredging fees. It was resolved to approve this, and after the sugar industry association submits the reasons to the meeting, separate petitions will be submitted. (5) Discussed the proposal by Committee Member Qing to re-assert the Shanghai Arsenal's creditor rights. It was resolved to publish a public notice stating that the disposal of the factory's assets shall be invalid until the Chamber of Commerce's creditor rights are resolved with consent.

The Silk Factory Labor Dispute in Zhabei Was Fully Resolved Through Mediation Yesterday 119

Disturbances Still Occurred in the Sixth District Yesterday Morning

Both Parties Signed Five Resolution Terms

The Labor Union Announced That Work Would Resume Uniformly Tomorrow Morning

Since the strike at the silk factories in the Fourth and Sixth Districts of Zhabei on the morning of the 5th, the factory owners and workers have failed to hold close negotiations for days. As a result, there have been several instances of resumed strikes after work had restarted. Meanwhile, a group of unemployed female workers have been causing disturbances everywhere, pressuring factories that have already resumed work to not work before a practical solution is achieved. This has led to unwarranted disturbances in the silk factory area for days. Fortunately, the police stations and police brigades in each district have been making great efforts to suppress the unrest, preventing any disasters. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, the Social Affairs Bureau convened both parties for mediation, which resulted in a satisfactory outcome. The original plan was to resume work today (the 9th), but because it is Sunday, factories typically have a day off, so it was decided that work will resume uniformly tomorrow morning. The events of yesterday are described below:

(Situation in Each District Yesterday) In the Sixth District of Zhabei, the silk factories were disturbed by female workers from the Wu Xing and Hong Da silk factories on the afternoon before yesterday, and they were unable to continue working and had to stop work again. Yesterday morning, the Sixth District Silk Weaving Industry Association still sent personnel to the factories as usual to advise the workers. At the same time, the Fourth Squadron of the Public Security Bureau and the police of the Fourth District also went out to protect the factories in front of the factory gates. As a result, the workers of each factory entered the factory to work one after another. Unexpectedly, the female workers of the Mao Feng and Qian Yuan factories on Changan Road suddenly started a disturbance, inciting all the female workers to stop work and leave the factory, and smashing the glass windows of the factory buildings. The factory had no choice but to stop the machines and let them go out. The female workers then swarmed to other factories that had already started working and shouted, firmly ordering them to strike and take uniform action. Although the police and the labor union tried to stop them, it was still ineffective. As a result, female workers from factories on Changan Road, Hengfeng Road, Meiyuan Road, and Gonghe Road were forced to leave the factories and strike again. The Fourth Squadron of the Public Security Bureau, upon hearing the news, quickly dispatched a large number of armed police to suppress the unrest at key intersections and ordered the female workers gathered in various places to disperse in batches. Unexpectedly, the female workers gathered again and swarmed to the Dayang Bridge and Tanziwan areas to cause disturbances. Fearing incidents, the factories automatically stopped work. As for the factories in the Fourth District, they remained temporarily closed during the day, and the sirens were not sounded. The female workers scattered in their homes, so the order was very good. Police officers were sent by the Public Security Bureau to guard the gates of the factories. The Zheng Feng and Yun Cheng factories were repairing their machines, and the situation was very quiet. As for those who were not affected by this incident and continued to work as usual, there were seven in the Sixth District: Hong Yu, Tian Sheng, Sheng Feng of Yan Jiage on Liuying Road, Mao Li of Tanjia Bridge, Xing Lun, Yu Feng of Gujia Bay, and Heng Cang of Miaotou. In the Fourth District, only Fu Lun Heng and Shuang Gong factories continued to work, and others in the concession areas also worked as usual.

(Mediation Officially Established) The Social Affairs Bureau specially convened a mediation committee at 10:00 AM yesterday to conduct mediation. The attendees included Huang Jinfan and Zhang Peishen from the Silk Factory Industry Association, Yang Gengti and Chen Xiu Pu from the Third, Fourth, and Sixth District Silk Weaving Industry Unions, and labor union supervisors and directors Le Xiaorong, Yuan Yunlong, Wu Suzhen, Liu Sanbao, Yan Aizhu, Yang Shumei, Chen Lianxi, Gu Xiaomei, Chen Yundi, Wu Xiubao, Pan Jingqiu, Wang Genbao, etc., and Fan Guoren from the Municipal Party Department's People's Training Section. The meeting was chaired by Wang Xianqing, Director of the Mediation Section of the Third Division, and Wang Zhiqin recorded the proceedings. First, the chairman announced that the labor side had requested the restoration of wages and benefits, and the bureau had sent personnel to investigate. Now, they have convened to conduct mediation, hoping that both parties will be open and honest so that they can jointly discuss solutions. The labor side stated that they are proposing to restore the wage to six jiao, the Sunday bonus to three jiao, the "shen gong" to four jiao, and to fulfill the previously agreed-upon treatment clauses. The capital side stated that there are 103 silk factories in the city, and less than half of them are currently open. Some of the leased factory bases are only for three months or six months and are temporary in nature. The labor side has suddenly gone on strike without following legal procedures, and it is inevitable that they have been incited by third parties. The factories are well aware of the workers' suffering, but they hope to cooperate with labor and capital and appropriately increase wages, but only for a period of three months. After repeated persuasion from the chairman and long-term consultations, the agreement was signed at 1:20 PM, and the mediation was completed. The mediation record was signed on the spot, stating that the right dispute party, for wage and other disputes, was convened by this committee for mediation, and both parties agreed to sign the following agreement: (1) The wages of all silk weaving female workers in the city will be restored to 4 jiao 5 fen from June, and the rest will be inferred. (2) The Sunday reward is 2 jiao per week, limited to July, August, and September (three months). (3) "Shen gong" is two "gong" per month, for both male and female employees (one "gong" for ten days, two "gong" for eighteen days). This will be temporarily set for three months, and if the market situation is the same as it is now after three months, it will continue to be issued. (4) The silkworm moth subsidy for employees will be issued monthly according to the usual salary, with a subsidy of 2 jiao per yuan. This will be temporarily set for three months, and if the market situation is no different from the current situation after three months, it will continue to be subsidized. (5) Workers from striking factories will be persuaded by the labor union to work as usual on the morning of the 10th of this month. This case has been agreed upon by representatives of both parties, and the signing of the mediation is deemed to be a collective agreement between the parties to the dispute (see the list of signatures above).

(Labor Union Announces Resumption of Work) The Third, Fourth, and Sixth District Silk Weaving Industry Union yesterday issued a notice to all workers stating that, regarding the issue of restoring treatment, this union has joined with other district unions to request the Social Affairs Bureau to mediate and resolve the matter. The main points of the clauses are extracted as follows: (1) The wages of female workers in the workshop will be restored to 5 jiao, and the rest will be inferred. (2) The Sunday reward is 2 jiao per week, limited to July, August, and September (three months). (3) "Shen gong" is two "gong" per month for both male and female employees. One "gong" for ten days, two "gong" for eighteen days. If you ask for leave for one day, deduct one "gong," one and a half "gong" for one and a half days, and two "gong" for two days. This will be temporarily set for three months, and if the market situation is the same as it is now after three months, it will continue to be issued. (4) The silkworm moth subsidy for employees will be issued monthly according to the usual salary, with a subsidy of 2 jiao per yuan. This will be temporarily set for three months, and if the market situation is no different from the current situation after three months, it will continue to be subsidized. The above items have been formally signed and it has been decided to start the car to work as usual next Monday. Please all workers go to the factory on time and as usual to work, and do not stay on the way. This is the most important thing. This notice is hereby given. July 8, 1933. At the same time, the three agencies of the Municipal Party Department, the Social Affairs Bureau, and the Public Security Bureau jointly issued a notice and posted it everywhere.

(Dispatching Police to Protect the Start of Work) The Silk Factory Industry Association yesterday notified its members that, in accordance with the mediation record of the Social Affairs Bureau, the Fourth and Sixth Districts of Zhabei will sound the sirens to start work uniformly on the morning of the 10th of this month. The Public Security Council decided to send additional armed police officers tomorrow morning to protect female workers from entering the factory to resume work in the silk factory areas such as Tiantong Road, Tianbao Road, and Hengfeng Road, and to prevent rioters from inciting workers. The Social Affairs Bureau will send cadres to various places to prevent the riots. The Third, Fourth, and Sixth District Silk Weaving Union decided to set out today and tomorrow morning with all the supervisors and directors to advise the workers and explain the situation. (Bailout of Detained Workers) During the labor unrest a few days ago, the Fifth Sub-bureau of the Public Security Bureau detained seven workers who threw stones and caused trouble: Gao Xiaowuzi, Chen Shuying, Zhao Di, Xiaowuzi, A'san, Wuzi, Chen A'er, and so on. In addition, Shen Xiaozuanzi was arrested when he was released from work the night before last. The sub-bureau prepared a document and transferred him to the main bureau for questioning. During yesterday morning's mediation, the labor side requested that all detained workers be released. The Social Affairs Bureau expressed its acceptance and promised to notify the Public Security Bureau that the labor union would be allowed to bail them out. Subsequently, the labor union prepared a document and requested the Public Security Bureau to release them.

Japan's Foreign Trade in the First Half of the Year 120

Excess of Imports, Excess of Exports to China

The Japanese Commercial Affairs Counselor's Office in Shanghai yesterday received a domestic telegram reporting that Japan's foreign trade in the first half of this year totaled 829,000,000 yen in exports, an increase of 59% over the same period last year, and 1,016,000,000 yen in imports, an increase of 24.2% over the same period last year. Comparing exports and imports, there was still an excess of imports of 186,000,000 yen, a decrease of 30% over the same period last year. The main export goods included cotton fabrics (183,000,000 yen), raw silk (167,000,000 yen), rayon fabrics (32,000,000 yen), silk fabrics (30,000,000 yen), flour (19,000,000 yen), socks (18,000,000 yen), canned or bottled food (17,000,000 yen), and porcelain (15,000,000 yen). The main import goods included cotton (327,000,000 yen), wool (82,000,000 yen), iron (73,000,000 yen), machinery (35,000,000 yen), kerosene (33,000,000 yen), beans (31,000,000 yen), and soybean cake (30,000,000 yen). (All figures are in Japanese yen.)

In May, Japan's trade with China totaled 9,000,000 yen in exports and 5,000,000 yen in imports, with an excess of exports of 4,000,000 yen. From January to May, Japan's trade surplus with China reached 19,000,000 yen (while China had a trade deficit), a decrease of 22% compared to the same period last year. In May, Japan's trade with Manchuria totaled 23,000,000 yen in exports and 15,000,000 yen in imports, with an excess of exports of 8,000,000 yen.

From January to May, Japan's trade surplus with Manchuria totaled 27,000,000 yen, while the same period last year had a deficit of 25,000,000 yen.

In the end, our army ran out of ammunition and was cut off from reinforcements, and finally suffered a disastrous defeat. Now they are still disintegrating into parts, lurking in various places, waiting for an opportunity to launch.

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Issued a Public Notice Yesterday Declaring the Mortgage Rights of the Arsenal 128

Has the Responsibility to Legally Eliminate Improper Infringements

Any Private Sale Is Invalid According to Law

Regarding the mortgage rights of the Shanghai Arsenal base, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce issued a public notice yesterday, stating that in 1925, the former Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, on behalf of the government, transferred a loan for the purpose of handling the dismissal of defeated soldiers and transporting supplies. With the approval of the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of the Army at that time, the base of the factory was used as a mortgage, and when the relocation of the factory was implemented and the base was sold, all land prices would be used to repay the principal and interest of the aforementioned loan first. The deed of the factory base and the guarantee letter from the old Ministry of the Army were held as proof. Upon the establishment of the Chamber of Commerce, all the rights and obligations of the former General Chamber of Commerce were legally assumed by the Chamber of Commerce. In May 1929, the current Ministry of Finance also presented a proposal to the Executive Yuan to maintain the original plan, and ordered the Ministry of Military and Political Affairs to be informed. According to the above circumstances, the Chamber of Commerce has the responsibility to legally eliminate improper infringements in the implementation of mortgage rights after the factory relocation is implemented. If someone sells the land privately, resulting in damage to the rights, it will be invalid according to law. It is hoped that both the grantor and the grantee will pay attention. This notice is hereby given.

Unprecedented Grand National Silk Exhibition Opens Today 130

Enthusiastic Participation Leads to Expanded Exhibition Space

Ms. Hu Die Inaugurates the Event at 1 PM

The China National Silk Exhibition will officially open at 1 PM this afternoon. All preparations and arrangements have been rushed to completion overnight by the preparatory office of the exhibition, in conjunction with the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce's Merchandise Exhibition Hall and the National Products Market. The venue and exhibition space are extremely grand. Details are as follows: (A Glimpse of the Venue)

The main venue is the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce's assembly hall, the largest public gathering place in Shanghai, with a capacity of over 3,200 spectators upstairs and downstairs. After three days and nights of decoration, it appears even more magnificent and spacious. At the entrance of the venue, banners proclaim "Promote National Silk, Recover Rights," and "Relieve People's Livelihood." On the large columns beside the banners are two couplets written by Wang Xiaolai, Vice President of the exhibition: "Five-colored patterns, joyfully become brocade embroidery; Seven-fold materials, greatly expand the plan;" and "Seeking others is not as good as seeking oneself; self-reliance to seek self-strengthening." Facing the entrance is the speaker's platform, with a large banner reading "China National Silk Exhibition" hanging in the center. To the left, it says, "Adopting foreign goods is economic suicide;" to the right, "Only national products can stop the leakage." Above the platform is a warning: "China is already impoverished and exhausted; people who are intoxicated by imported goods, wake up quickly!" On both sides are "Consolidating silk industry financial institutions is indirectly supporting the silk industry;" and "The industrial and financial sectors should unite to promote national products." Under the platform is a slogan: "The exhibition is to leave a lasting and profound impression on the public." (Exhibition Condition)

At the entrance of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce and the Merchandise Exhibition Hall, a decorative archway is made of pine branches, with the nine characters "China National Silk Exhibition" made of electric lights. After entering the main gate, large paintings depicting national suffering are hung along the road, alarming viewers. There are also slogans about promoting national silk, pasted all over the walls. Beside the iron gate hangs a couplet: "National clothing, please come in; foreign clothing, roll out," which is straightforward and pleases the viewers. (Expanded Exhibition)

The exhibition space was originally set in the third floor of the Exhibition Hall, with a total of 115 display cases of three types: A, B, and C. Unexpectedly, before the 6th, the number of display cases required by the registered manufacturers had already exceeded 150. After the 6th, more manufacturers continued to sign up to participate. Therefore, the original location was insufficient. The Exhibition Hall managed to vacate part of the fourth floor, adding 54 display cases, for a total of 169 display cases, the largest scale since the National Silk Exhibition began.

(General Overview of Decoration)

After the manufacturers spent the entire day of the 7th decorating, forty to fifty percent of the displays were completed by noon on the 8th. The remaining fifty to sixty percent required all-night work on the 8th due to the temporary addition of electric lights. At noon on the 8th, a reporter from the New Sound News Agency made a preliminary tour, seeing that the entrance to the exhibition hall was the Shanghai Silk Industry Bank office. Winding inward, the new products of the Wah Sun Dyeing Factory were beautiful and eye-catching. The Pharmacy Reports to the Police for Investigation

At 9:20 PM the day before yesterday, a man of about 30 years old, wearing a white short shirt and pants, suddenly threw a paper package at the counter of the Pacific Pharmacy at 119 North Szechuan Road (Yokohama Bridge).
